<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="obstetrical-emergencies">OBSTETRICAL EMERGENCIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obstetrical-emergencies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="post-partum-heamorrhage-pph">POST PARTUM HEAMORRHAGE (PPH)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-partum-heamorrhage-pph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Def: It's the bleeding after delivery of the baby amounting to 500 mls or more per vaginally or 1 litre through ceaserian section or ay amount affecting the mother's condition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-pph">TYPES OF PPH;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-pph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two types of PPH;</p>
<ol>
<li>Primary PPH</li>
<li>Secondary PPH</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-pph">PRIMARY PPH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-pph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Def: It's the bleeding after delivery of the baby amounting to 500 mls or more vaginal or 1 litre through ceaserian section or ay amount affecting the mother's condition occurring within 24 hours after birth</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-pph">Causes of PPH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-pph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are four causes: (4Ts)</p>
<ol>
<li>T-Tone (Atonic uterus) – most common</li>
<li>T-Trauma (e.g. tear, ruptured uterus)</li>
<li>T-Tissue (Retained products of conception)</li>
<li>T-Thrombin (thrombocytopenia – clotting disorders)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-atonic-uterus">1. Atonic uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-atonic-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Def: This is a situation where the uterus fails to contract after delivery of the baby.</p>
<p>NB/ The commonest cause of primary PPH</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors-to-atonic-uterus">Predisposing factors to Atonic uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-to-atonic-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Multiple pregnancy</p>
<p>This is as a result of over distension of the uterus</p>
<p>b. Polyhydromnous</p>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>This is a condition where is excessive amniotic fluid in the uterus either or equal to 1500ml. this contributes to over distension of uterus leading to atonic uterus</p>
<p>c. Big baby</p>
<p>This causes over distension of the uterus leading to uterus Atomy.</p>
<p>d. Prolonged labour</p>
<p>It exposes uterine muscles to fatigue reducing the ability to contract after the delivery of the baby causing uterine atony</p>
<p>e. Fibroids</p>
<p>It reduces the ability of the uterus to contract (being an abnormal growth/mass in the uterus) after the delivery of the baby</p>
<p>f. Full bladder</p>
<p>A full bladder competes for space with the contracting uterus which prevents the uterus from contracting fully thus causing atonic uterus.</p>
<p>g. Previous caesarean section CCS</p>
<p>The previous as scar usually heals with a formation of a fibrous tissues; the fibrosis reduces the ability of the uterus to contract leading to uterus atony.</p>
<p>h. Multiply parity</p>
<p>Every time you conceive the placenta site changes for convenience.</p>
<p>Every previous placental site heals with fibrosis. The more placental site the more the myometrium is replaced with fibrous tissue and this result to uterine atony after the delivery of the baby</p>
<p>i. Placenta previa</p>
<p>This is a placenta on the lower uterine segment; the ability of the uterus to contract and close the placental site of the uterus segment is low. It is as a result of fewer myometrium on the lower uterine segment leading to haemorrhage.</p>
<p>j. Placenta abruption</p>
<p>With placenta abruption there is a formation of rect ro-placental dot. Blood from the dot leaks or its absorbed into the myometrium, resulting into a couvelewr uterus or uterine myometra. This will lead to inability of myometrium to contract resulting to uterine atony.</p>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>3</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>k. Precipitate labour</p>
<p>This is abnormal short labour characterized by contractions with no retractions, after delivery of the baby the uterus fails to contract due to poor muscle co-ordination during labour to uterine atony.</p>
<p>l. Drugs</p>
<p>Use of drugs that affect the contractility of the uterus e.g. Anesthetic drug, Anticonvulsant e.g. MgSo4</p>
<p>m. Mismanagement of 3rd stage of labour</p>
<p>This includes even the failure or delay to administer syntocinon after the birth of the baby as required.</p>
<p>n. Over massaging of the abdomen.</p>
<p>Massage brings muscle confusion.</p>
<p>o. Over use of oxygen will lead to failure of oxytonic to cause contraction of the uterus.</p>
<p>Once the uterus is exposed to sintocinon several times the effectiveness of the drug goes down. The oxytocin receptors on the uterus fail to work effectively.</p>
<p>p. Retained placenta</p>
<p>This is when retained products of conception e.g. placenta, clots, membranes have not been delivered. This is one of the most common causes of uterine atony.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis-of-an-atonic-uterus">Diagnosis of an Atonic uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis-of-an-atonic-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Excess bleeding after the delivery of the body
b. Uterus feels softly and boggy, distended.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nb">NB<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>All women with risk factors to atonic uterus should receive prophylactic management to the mother about an atonic uterus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-postpartum-hemorrhage-with-atonic-uterus">Management of postpartum hemorrhage with Atonic uterus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-postpartum-hemorrhage-with-atonic-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Shout for help, Dr ABC</li>
<li>Reassure the mother.</li>
<li>Massage the uterus to expel clots</li>
<li>Empty bladder</li>
<li>Remove clots if any</li>
<li>Give oxytocin if not given or repeat 10ru</li>
<li>Fix an iv access preferably with large bone cannula gauge 16-18.</li>
<li>Collect blood sample for investigation, GXM, dotting time platelet count Hb</li>
</ol>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>
<p>Start the mother on syntocinon 20-40 IU in 1000ml of normal saline and run at a rate of 60 drops for the 1st one litre. Then 20 - 40 IU in 1000ml of normal saline to run at 40 drops per minute.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer misoprostal or cytotec 800mg start rectal for PPM (4 table for mouth for induction)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>administer ergometrine 0.2 mgs intravenously every 15 minutes to a maximum of 1 gram</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer prostaglandin F2 1-2 mg start intramyometrial through abdomen to the endometrium.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perform bi- manual compression of the uterus either internal or external.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>With internal bi- manual compression one head on the fundus and other on cervix</li>
<li>With external bi- manual compression, one hand is on the abdomen targeting the posterior aspect of the uterus while the other hand is abdomen again targeting the uterus anteriorly. Pressure is applied to compress the uterus.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="14">
<li>Baloon temponade can be done.</li>
<li>Perform an aortic compression</li>
<li>A B- lych suture can be applied in theatre.</li>
<li>If bleeding is more do total or subtotal hysterectomy</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="supportive-management">Supportive management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supportive-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Observe the mother closely 15 min for TPR, blood pressure putting more emphases on pulse.</li>
<li>Ensure that the mother is warm</li>
<li>You can consider transfusion</li>
<li>Observe infection prevention procedures.</li>
<li>Encourage breastfeeding</li>
<li>Administer broad spectrum antibiotic prophylactically.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-trauma">2. TRAUMA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-trauma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Def: This is injury to genital tract/reproductive organ following delivery of the baby leading to haemorrhage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Perineal tear. (tight and rigid perineum)</li>
<li>Big baby</li>
<li>Cervical tear</li>
<li>Malpresentation e.g. breech</li>
</ol>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>

<ol start="5">
<li>Malposition</li>
<li>Instrumental vaginal delivery e.g. vacuum delivery</li>
<li>Assisted vaginal delivery</li>
<li>Massage</li>
<li>External and internal cephalic version.</li>
<li>Mismanagement of labour (fail to support the perineum)</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-perineal-tears">Classification of perineal tears<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-perineal-tears" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. 1st Degree – it involves the vaginal mucosa
B. 2nd degree – it involves the vaginal mucosa and muscles
C. 3rd degree – involves vaginal mucosa and muscle and the anal sphincter
D. 4th degree – vaginal mucosa, muscles and anal sphincter and anterior wall of the rectum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-repair-to-perineal-tear">Principles of repair to perineal tear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-repair-to-perineal-tear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Observe infection prevention technique
ii. Us minimal suture
iii. Achieve haemostasis
iv. Pain management, adequate analgesics
v. Prophylactic; PRN (where technique)
vi. Good exposure/ view of the tear.
vii. Type 3 and 4 repair in theatre</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-pph-secondary-to-trauma">Management of PPH secondary to trauma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-pph-secondary-to-trauma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Shout for help, DR, ABC</li>
<li>IV access, fix large bone cannula, 16-18 gauge</li>
<li>Investigations; GXM, blood dotting time</li>
<li>Keep mother warm</li>
<li>Observations, TPR BP.</li>
<li>Repair the tear</li>
<li>Observe principals of perineal repair.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-education-after-repair">Health education after repair.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-education-after-repair" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Observe personal hygiene.</li>
<li>Clean with warm saline water. remember not hot saline saturated water otherwise it may interfere with healing process.</li>
<li>Delay sexual intercourse until healing takes place.</li>
<li>Avoid saline</li>
<li>Avoid constipation</li>
<li>Remind the mother that the suture used if absorbable then there will be removal of stitches.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-thrombocytopenia-clotting-disorders">3. Thrombocytopenia'- Clotting disorders<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-thrombocytopenia-clotting-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is bleeding after delivery of the baby due to clothing disorders</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Intra uterine fetal death (IUFD)
ii. Severe pre-eclampsia (PET)
iii. Amniotic fluid embolism; if amniotic fluid goes to maternal circulation
iv. Antipartum haemorrhage due to placenta abruption
v. Drugs e.g. Heparin for treatment of coagulant disorders
vi. Septicemia secondary to severe haemorrhage
vii. Massive transfusion
viii. Haemophilia</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Excessive bleeding
ii. Low platelet count less than 150
iii. Prolonged bedside clotting time above 11 minutes</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Dr ABC, shout for help
B. Iv access
C. Investigation
D. Observation, temperature, blood pressure, pulse.
E. Keep the mother warm</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specific-management">Specific management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Give fresh frozen plasma
ii. Transfuse with most fresh blood
iii. Give intrinsic factors or synthetic fibrinogen 0.8mg stat. Cryoprecipitate boasts the intrinsic factors
iv. Give clotting factors (platelets)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-retained-placenta">4. RETAINED PLACENTA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-retained-placenta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition- This is a condition where after the delivery of the baby the placenta fails to be delivered spontaneously within 30 minutes.</p>
<p>Occurs to 0.8- 1.2% of deliveries.</p>
<p>15 re- 20% of maternal death as a result of pph is due to retained placenta.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>atonic uterus</li>
<li>placenta separated but trapped in cervix</li>
<li>abnormal placentation (accrete, incrata, pancreta)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>previous surgery or trauma</li>
<li>uterine abnormality</li>
<li>preterm deliveries</li>
<li>poor skills placenta removal</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>explain to the mother</li>
<li>reassure</li>
<li>manage uterus</li>
<li>empty bladder</li>
<li>Start sintocinon 10 units intramuscularly and 5 units intravenously.</li>
<li>perform manual removal - skill</li>
<li>administer antibiotics</li>
<li>In case placenta cannot be delivered e.g. in placenta pancetta, reduce cord, ligate and retain</li>
<li>Administer methotrixate to avoid malignancy.</li>
<li>once out explore uterine cavity and perform placental examination</li>
<li>Encourage breastfeeding.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Haemorrhage</li>
<li>Sepsis of</li>
<li>Risk of cancer</li>
<li>Maternal death</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cord-prolapse">CORD PROLAPSE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cord-prolapse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Def: This is a condition where the cord is lying ahead of the presenting part and membranes are ruptured</p>
<p>Incidence: 1 in every 300 pregnancies is likely to complicate with cord prolapse.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-bef24231.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<p>Cord presentation; this is a condition where the cord is a head of presenting part and membranes are intact</p>
<p>Occult cord presentation; this is when the cord is on the side of the presenting part, neither the head/ buttocks nor the cord is leading.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="predisposing-factors">PREDISPOSING FACTORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-long-cord">1. Long cord<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-long-cord" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Any cord above 60 cm is considered log cord. It can always take advantage of its length and find itself ahead of the presenting part.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-polyhydromnous">2. Polyhydromnous<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-polyhydromnous" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is presence of excessive amniotic fluid in the uterus. The risk for cord prolapsed is high in case of spontaneous rupture of membranes. The force exerted by the gush of the amniotic fluid sweeps the cord and brings it ahead of the presenting part..</p>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>

<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Premature rapture of membranes</li>
</ol>
<p>The head is rarely engaged and the cord can find space and lead the presenting part</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>A high presenting part</li>
</ol>
<p>There is room for cord to present when the mother goes into labour with head still high.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Malpresentation</li>
</ol>
<p>This is when there is a abnormal presentation e.g. shoulder presentation, breech e.t.c. abnormal presentations are associated with poor fitting presenting part to the pelvis. That situation creates space for the cord to find its way ahead of the presenting part.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Placenta previa</li>
</ol>
<p>The placenta is already on the lower uterine segment so the cord. This gives advantage of the cord to be ahead of the presenting part.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Contracted pelvis</li>
</ol>
<p>A contracted pelvis will not favour the presenting part to fit well. It may allow some space for the cord to present.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Multiple pregnancy</li>
</ol>
<p>There is more than one fetus in the uterus. The risk for cord prolapse increases from the one fetus to the other as they are being born. In case of twin pregnancy the second twin carries a greater risk.</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>low birth weight</li>
</ol>
<p>A low birth weight &lt;2500 predisposes to cord presentation. this condition is almost similar to prematurity.</p>
<p>DIAGNOSIS</p>
<p>i. Visibility of a cord on vaginal inspection.
ii. Palpation of a cord with ruptured membranes ahead of presenting part.
iii. Suspect with abnormal fetal heart after rapture of membranes
iv. ultra sound</p>
<p>MANAGEMENT</p>
<p>NOTE:</p>
<p>In the management of cord prolapsed with a live fetus we aim at quick delivery of the baby using the quickest method possible. Guidelines suggest that any cord prolapse occurring during first stage of labour the mode of delivery should be ceaserian section. During second stage consider vaginal delivery unless contraindicated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-determining-management-of-cord-prolapse">Factors determining management of cord prolapse;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-determining-management-of-cord-prolapse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i. Whether the cord is pulsating or not
ii. Adequacy of the pelvis
iii. Stage of labour
iv. The level of health facility – Bemonc or Cemonc</p>
<ul>
<li>During the management of cord prolapse, assess if the cord is outside the birth canal clean it with warm normal saline or hibitane and pack with clean gauze back into the birth canal.</li>
<li>Reassure the mother and the relatives.</li>
<li>If it occurred at home while undergoing home delivery thank the mother for making the decision to come to the hospital.</li>
<li>Perform abdominal palpation to confirm the lie is of the fetus. It must be longitudinal. If it is transverse prepare for referral if in a basic obstetrical care facility or ceaserian section if in a comprehensive obstetrical care facility.</li>
<li>Always relieve pressure of the cord. The fetus may not survive beyond 10 minutes with cord compression.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-relieving-pressure-off-the-cord-pressure">Methods of relieving pressure off the cord pressure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-relieving-pressure-off-the-cord-pressure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Knee elbow position</li>
<li>Raise the foot of the bed – reverse tendelsburg position.</li>
<li>Counter pressure</li>
<li>Exaggerated sims position</li>
<li>Fill the bladder with N/S</li>
<li>Tocolytics; give mg50s, 4gm IV of 20% or sulbutamol.</li>
</ol>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-in-a-basic-emergency-maternal-and-newborn-care-bemonc-facility">MANAGEMENT IN A BASIC EMERGENCY MATERNAL AND NEWBORN CARE (BEMoNC) FACILITY.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-in-a-basic-emergency-maternal-and-newborn-care-bemonc-facility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="during-first-stage-of-labour">During first stage of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#during-first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>It is an obstetric emergency. Do not start any partograph as per the guidelines.</li>
<li>If the <strong>cord is pulsating</strong> and <strong>pelvis is adequate</strong> refer the mother to a comprehensive obstetrical care facility. This is according to the guidelines.</li>
<li>If the <strong>cord is pulsating</strong> and <strong>pelvis is not adequate</strong> refer the mother to a comprehensive obstetrical care facility. Inform the mother and relatives about the delivery option which is caesarian section.</li>
</ul>
<p>As you are referring the woman since the fetus is alive do the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Establish intra venous access.</li>
<li>Take blood samples</li>
<li>Start the woman on intravenous fluids preferable normal saline.</li>
<li>Put her on oxygen by mask</li>
<li>Prevent any pressure to the cord by presenting part by taking the following measures;</li>
<li>Position the mother in the either of the following positions as explained earlier to relieve pressure off the cord;</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Reverse tendelberge position</li>
<li>Exaggerated sim,s position</li>
<li>Knee chest position</li>
</ol>
<p>OR use the manourvers to relieve pain</p>
<ol>
<li>Fill bladder with normal saline approximately 500mls- 1000mls.</li>
<li>Apply counter pressure with your examination fingers in the vagina during every contraction.</li>
<li>Administer tocolytics magnesium sulphate or salbutamol</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: The cause for occlusion of cord vessels is either <strong>physical compression</strong> OR <strong>low temperatures</strong>.</p>
<ul>
<li>In case she approaches second stage allow her to push if the fetus is in longitudinal lie.</li>
<li>Expect to receive an asphyxiated baby.</li>
</ul>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; If cord is not pulsating, pelvis is adequate and fetus in longitudinal lie, allow the mother to bear down. Counsel her to expect a dead fetus.
&gt; If cord is not pulsating ad pelvis is not adequate refer the mother to a comprehensive care facility for further management to include destructive operation/ embryotomy.
&gt; In case the fetus is dead and the mother has very strong uterine contractions with an inadequate pelvis you can administer tocolytics e.g. magnesium sulphate 4gms of 20% intravenously start dose as you refer.
&gt; Always remember to carry with you a delivery pack during referral.
&gt; Inform the referral hospital about the condition of the mother.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-2da2bdee.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-during-second-stage-of-labour-in-a-bemonc">Management during second stage of labour in a BEMoNC.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-second-stage-of-labour-in-a-bemonc" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>&gt; If the lie longitudinal, fetal heart present, pelvis is adequate and in second stage of labour, plan for a quick delivery and give an episiotomy. Assisted vaginal delivery (AVD) can be applied to fasten 2nd stage.. Prepare for resuscitation
&gt; If fetal heart is present, pelvis is inadequate and lie is longitudinal refer the mother to a comprehensive care facility. Give normal saline or ringers lactate. Put the mother on oxygen.
&gt; Carry with you a delivery and resuscitation pack.
&gt; Monitor fetal heart rate ¼ hourly and inform the comprehensive facility to prepare for an obstetrical emergency.</p>

<p>If the pelvis is inadequate, cord is not pulsating, inform the mother about the condition. Refer her to a comprehensive care facility for embryotomy or decapitation.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-in-a-comprehensive-obstetric-and-newborn-care-cemonc-health-facility">MANAGEMENT IN A COMPREHENSIVE OBSTETRIC AND NEWBORN CARE (CEMONC) HEALTH FACILITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-in-a-comprehensive-obstetric-and-newborn-care-cemonc-health-facility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="during-first-stage-of-labour">During first stage of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#during-first-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>If cord is pulsating, pelvis is adequate and lie is longitudinal position the mother to relieve pressure off the cord and prepare for emergency ceaserian section. Give intravenous fluids, oxygen via mask, investigations can be done and monitor fetal heart rate vigilantly.</li>
<li>In case the cord is not pulsating, pelvis is adequate and lie longitudinal counsel her and let her undergo normal labour aimed at vaginal delivery unless there is a contraindication.</li>
<li>In case the cord is not pulsating, pelvis is inadequate and lie longitudinal or not counsel her and let her undergo embryotomy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="during-second-stage-of-labour">During second stage of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#during-second-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>If cord is pulsating and pelvis is adequate give a generous episiotomy and urge the mother to push. Assisted vaginal delivery (AVD) can be applied to hasten second stage of labour. Prepare for resuscitation as you anticipate receiving an asphyxiated baby.</li>
<li>If cord is pulsating and pelvis is inadequate prepare for emergency c/s. meanwhile administer oxygen via mask, relieve pressure off the cord and rehydrate the mother.</li>
<li>If cord not pulsating and pelvis is adequate prepare the mother to accept a dead and deliver baby by spontaneous vaginal delivery unless contraindicated.</li>
</ul>

<ul>
<li>If cord not pulsating and pelvis is inadequate prepare the mother to accept a dead and deliver baby by embryotomy/ decapitation.</li>

<p>NB: It is approximated that 10 minutes is a long time for the baby to stand cord compression without much complications.</p>
<p>Prognosis of cord presentation is good in breech presentation as compared to cephalic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="complications-of-cord-prolapse">Complications of cord prolapse<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-cord-prolapse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Fetal distress</li>
<li>Maternal distress</li>
<li>Fetal death</li>
<li>Maternal mortality</li>
<li>Fetal hypoxia</li>
<li>Asphyxia neonatorum</li>
<li>Brain damage</li>
<li>Still birth</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uterine-inversion">UTERINE INVERSION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uterine-inversion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is when the uterus turns inner side out i.e. inner side of the fundus into the vaginal canal.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Mismanagement of 3rd stage of labour</li>
<li>Excessive fundal pressure</li>
<li>Short cord</li>
<li>Precipitate labour</li>
<li>Polyhydrominous</li>
<li>Prolonged labour</li>
<li>Fundal myoma</li>
<li>Ante partum use of magnesium sulphate</li>
<li>Primiparity</li>
<li>Fundal placentation</li>
<li>Abnormal placentation</li>
<li>History of uterine inversion.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is according to <strong>time of onset</strong> and <strong>severity</strong>.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-according-to-time-of-onset">Classification according to time of onset<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-according-to-time-of-onset" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Acute inversion</li>
<li>Sub- acute inversion</li>
<li>Chronic inversion</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-acute-inversion">1. Acute inversion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-acute-inversion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Occurs after birth and before the cervical ring closes</li>
<li>Usually within 24 hours after delivery.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-sub-acute-inversion">2. Sub acute inversion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-sub-acute-inversion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Occurs after cervical ring has closed</li>
<li>Occurs after 24 hours after birth of the baby to 4 weeks</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-chronic-inversion">3. Chronic inversion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-chronic-inversion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Occurs after 4 weeks after delivery.</li>
<li>It is associated with disease e.g. CA.</li>
</ul>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Classification according to severity</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Incomplete/1st degree
Uterine inverts but lies in the uterine cavity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Complete uterine inversion/ 2nd degree
Fundus of the uterus goes beyond the external OS of the cervix. It is in the vaginal canal but not beyond the hymen. It's palpable on vaginal examination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prolapsed uterine inversion/ 3rd degree
Inverted uterus goes beyond the vaginal introits.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Total uterine inversion/ 4th degree
Involves vaginal walls and the uterus both seen at the vulva. Associated with CA cervix and Peurperial sepsis.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Diagnosis</p>
<p>a) Visible in case of uterine prolapse.
b) Palpated inverted uterus
c) Haemorrhage
d) Felt in the vagina in case of complete inversion
e) Severe hypotension with other signs of shock
f) Fundus missing on abdominal palpation
g) Ultra sound can be done</p>
<p>3.5 Management.</p>
<p>The principles of management of uterine inversion are;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Treatment of shock/ stabilizing the mother from hemorrhage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Replacement of the uterus</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This is an obstetric emergency.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Call for help</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Reassure the mother</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fix two large bore cannulars</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Resuscitate with intravenous fluids</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer oxygen</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Take blood for GXM and order for fresh blood</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Elevate the foot of the bed</li>
<li>Sedate the mother with pethidine.</li>
<li>Take vital signs ¼ hourly</li>
<li>Clean the uterus with hibitane or warm normal saline and pack with gauze.</li>
<li>Discontinue uterotonic therapy.</li>
<li>If the uterus is inverted and contracted at the same time making replacement difficult halothane can be administered.</li>
<li>Replace the uterus immediately manual (Johnsons manouvre) or inflate with normal saline (hydrostatic manouvre)</li>
<li>Administer syntocinon immediately after correction has been done.</li>
<li>The mother should be started on broad spectrum antibiotics</li>
<li>If the maneuvers were unsuccessful consider surgical interventions to include laparatomy and OR hysterectomy.</li>
<li>In case the uterus is replaced and the woman is still bleeding manage as PPH.</li>
<li>A pap smear can be taken to rule out cancer</li>
<li>Subsequent pregnancies are also at risk so let the woman attend clinic early and give history of uterine inversion.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Primary post partum haemorrhage</li>
<li>Infection</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Shock</li>
<li>Gangrene formation</li>
<li>Paralytic ileus</li>
<li>Infertility</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ruptured-uterus">RUPTURED UTERUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ruptured-uterus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is a tear in the wall of the uterus.</p>
<p>It is one of the serious obstetrical emergency though can be prevented.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types">Types<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Complete rapture</li>
<li>Incomplete rapture</li>
<li>Dehiscence</li>
</ul>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>I. Complete rupture</p>
<p>This is when the tear involves all the three layers of the uterus i.e. endometrium, myometrium, and perimetrium and sometimes plus peritoneum.</p>
<p>II. Incomplete rupture</p>
<p>This is the tear which involves endometrium and myometrium.</p>
<p>III. Dehiscence</p>
<p>This is when there is a tear involving the endometrium. In most cases this may go undiagnosed.</p>
<p>Predisposing factors</p>
<ol>
<li>Polyhydrominous</li>
<li>Multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Pregnancy occurring within 6 months after a CS (fresh scar)</li>
<li>Obstetric manipulation e.g. external cephalic version</li>
<li>Previous classical scar in labour</li>
<li>Malpresentation</li>
<li>Ignored labour.</li>
</ol>
<p>4.4 Causes of ruptured uterus</p>
<ol>
<li>Obstructed labour – shirodikar stitch in labour, cervical dystocia
1.2 Excessive use of oxytocin, especially in previous scar</li>
<li>Intra-uterine manipulation</li>
<li>Forceps deliveries and vacuum extraction</li>
<li>Multiparity</li>
<li>Trauma e.g. in accidents</li>
<li>Perforation of pregnant uterus leading to rapture during subsequent pregnancy</li>
</ol>
<p>4.5 Signs and symptoms.</p>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>The signs are categorized in to two i.e. early and late signs and signs indicating rupture has occurred.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-5-1-early-signs">4.5.1 Early signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-5-1-early-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Scar pain and tenderness in previous scar mother</li>
<li>Fresh per vaginal bleeding</li>
<li>Cervix does not open despite effective contractions</li>
<li>Increased pulse rate</li>
<li>Previous strong contractions cease abruptly</li>
<li>Presenting part is high despite strong contractions</li>
<li>Early rupture of membranes</li>
<li>Cervix appears like an “empty sleeve”</li>
<li>Fetal heart deceleration</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-5-2-late-signs">4.5.2 Late signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-5-2-late-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Dehydration</li>
<li>Ketosis (excessive metabolism of protein)</li>
<li>Severe pain</li>
<li>Poor urinary output and could be blood stained</li>
<li>Uterus is moulded around the fetus</li>
<li>Formation of a bundles ring</li>
<li>Contraction which do not relax in between contraction</li>
<li>Vagina hot and dry</li>
<li>Presenting part is high, wedged and immobile</li>
<li>Excessive moulding</li>
<li>Capput succedaneum</li>
<li>Mother is exhausted and appeals for help</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-5-3-signs-indicating-rupture">4.5.3 Signs indicating rupture<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-5-3-signs-indicating-rupture" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Feeling of a sharp pain during rupture</li>
<li>Mother feels something has given way fetal parts palpable in the abdomen</li>
<li>Sudden collapse</li>
<li>Contractions cease</li>
<li>Fetal heart rate disappears.</li>
<li>Fetal parts easily palpated of the abdomen and outside the uterus.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-6-management">4.6 Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-6-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Call for help and resuscitate mother</li>
<li>Elevate the feet of the mother</li>
<li>Start on IV infusion of N/S</li>
<li>Inform theatre and prepare for emergency CS</li>
<li>Prepare the mother for C/S</li>
<li>Inform and reassure her and relatives</li>
<li>Take blood for GXM and at least 2 units ready</li>
<li>Repair or hysterectomy done depending on the degree of tears</li>
<li>Counsel her not to conceive before 2 years are over if no hysterectomy was done</li>
<li>If hysterectomy was done counsel her not to expect another baby or menses.</li>
<li>ct management of postnatal mother</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-7-complications">4.7 COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-7-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-7-1-complications-to-the-mother">4.7.1 Complications to the mother<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-7-1-complications-to-the-mother" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Peritonitis</li>
<li>septicemia</li>
<li>urinary tract infection</li>
<li>renal failure</li>
<li>paralytic ileus</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Amniotic fluid embolism</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-7-2-complications-to-the-baby">4.7.2 Complications to the baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-7-2-complications-to-the-baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Birth asphyxia</li>
<li>still birth</li>
<li>neonatal death</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-8-prevention">4.8 Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-8-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>encourage women to attend clinic</li>
<li>discourage the community on use of herbs</li>
<li>All mothers with risk factors to be referred to hospital</li>
<li>Monitor labour by use of partograph</li>
<li>Early recognition of signs of obstruction and rapture of uterus</li>
<li>Diagnosis of contracted pelvis</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="5-0-amniotic-fluid-embolism-afe">5.0 AMNIOTIC FLUID EMBOLISM (AFE)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-0-amniotic-fluid-embolism-afe" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-1-definition">5.1 Definition.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-1-definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a rare but potential catastrophic condition which occurs when amniotic fluid enters the maternal circulation via the uterus or placental site forming an embolus which obstructs one of the pulmonary arterioles or alveolar capillaries. Be on the lookout, you may lose a woman who was health and with no signs of pending complication.</p>
<p>Remember amniotic fluid is rich in thromboplastin</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-2-pathophysiology">5.2 Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-2-pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The body responds in two phases:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Initial phase</li>
<li>Secondary phase</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="initial-phase-pulmonary-phase">Initial phase (pulmonary phase)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#initial-phase-pulmonary-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There is going to be pulmonary vasospasms causing</p>
<p>a) Hypoxia
b) Hypertension
c) Cardiopulmonary collapse</p>
<ul>
<li>50% of patients die during this phase</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="secondary-phase-hemorrhagic-phase">Secondary phase (hemorrhagic phase)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-phase-hemorrhagic-phase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This phase will be characterized by:</p>
<p>a) Left ventricular failure
b) Pulmonary oedema
c) Coagulatory disorder which will be followed by massive hemorrhage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-3-predisposing-factors">5.3 Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-3-predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Placental abruption</li>
</ul>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Perforation or ruptured uterus</li>
<li>Precipitate labour</li>
<li>Intra-uterine fetal manipulations</li>
<li>Caesarian section</li>
<li>Trauma</li>
<li>Termination of pregnancy</li>
<li>Manual removal of retained placenta</li>
<li>Obstetrical procedures e.g. amniotic transfusion, internal podalic version etc.</li>
<li>Over stimulation of the uterus by use of oxytocic drugs or prostaglandins</li>
<li>Advanced age</li>
<li>Associated with male fetus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-4-signs-and-symptoms">5.4 Signs and symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-4-signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cardiopulmonary arrest</li>
<li>Sudden onset of maternal respiratory distress syndrome</li>
<li>Turtumus laboured breathing</li>
<li>Maternal hypotension (sudden with loss of diastolic pressure)</li>
<li>Uterine atony</li>
<li>Collapse then followed by convulsions (seizures) with cyanosis</li>
<li>Blood coagulation disorder</li>
<li>Severe chest pain</li>
<li>Pulmonary oedema</li>
<li>Fetal brandycardia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-5-management-emergency-action">5.5 Management - Emergency action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-5-management-emergency-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Any of the above is indicative of an acute emergency as the mother is likely in a state of collapse.</li>
<li>Shout for help from a senior person.</li>
<li>Start resuscitation immediately</li>
<li>Establish intravenous access.</li>
<li>Rehydrate the mother with normal saline or ringers lactate</li>
<li>Aim at early delivery of the baby if still inside</li>
<li>Provide intensive care (nurse in ICU)</li>
<li>Prop up the mother and administer oxygen</li>
<li>Take blood for grouping and cross match</li>
<li>Contact the anesthetist in case of GA and cardiac problem</li>
<li>Administer aminophyline and hydrocortisone slowly to reduce bronchospasms</li>
<li>Transfuse with fresh blood slowly and administer fibrinogen</li>
</ul>
<p>Promoting safe motherhood</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
