<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications-effects-associated-with-twin-pregnancy">Complications/ effects associated with twin pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-effects-associated-with-twin-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Exaggeration of minor disorders e.g. vomiting, high levels of HCG hormone.</li>
<li>Anaemia due to high fetal demand (iron, folic, vit B12 deficiency)</li>
<li>Polyhydromnious in monochorionic.</li>
<li>Congenital disorders e.g. congenital cardiac diseases, down syndrome e.t.c.</li>
<li>Increased pressure symptoms</li>
<li>Predisposes to conditions like Pre-eclampsia is common</li>
<li>Premature labour due to over distention of abdomen.</li>
<li>Premature rupture of membranes due to pressure in the uterus</li>
</ul>
<p>Retained twin due to relaxation of the uterus</p>
<ul>
<li>Prematurity due to premature labour</li>
<li>Cord prolapsed with second twin</li>
<li>Intra uterine growth restriction associated with competition for nutrition</li>
<li>PPH due to uterus exhaustion especially atonic uterus.</li>
<li>Prolonged labour – due to malpresentation and poor uterine action</li>
<li>psychological effect (positive/ negative)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rhesus-incompatibility">RHESUS INCOMPATIBILITY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rhesus-incompatibility" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Rhesus factor is a protein bound in red blood cells. When you have that protein you are termed as <strong>rhesus positive</strong>. When you don't have it you are considered <strong>rhesus negative</strong>. Naturally majority of the population is rhesus positive.</p>
<p>When the woman is rhesus negative there is likelihood that the husband could be rhesus positive.</p>
<p>Risk develops when the woman is rhesus negative and is carrying a baby who happens to be rhesus positive.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Abortion</li>
<li>Miscarriage</li>
<li>Ante partum hemorrhage</li>
<li>Amniocentesis</li>
<li>Trauma</li>
<li>Chorionic villi aspiration</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Serum bilirubin level</li>
<li>Rhesus factor</li>
<li>Hemolytic process</li>
<li>Antibodies (direct and indirect coombs)</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Always aim at prevention.</p>
<ul>
<li>Prenatally take a blood sample from the mother and check if the mother has developed antibodies against rhesus positive blood.</li>
<li>Antenatally test the husband to confirm whether rhesus positive or negative. If the husband is rhesus positive then the mother is at risk. In case the rhesus factor of the husband remains unknown consider the woman at risk since the greater population is usually rhesus positive.</li>
<li>Administer anti-D profilactically at 28-32 weeks gestation. This is due to the higher risk of fetal and maternal blood mixing associated to the events of the placenta at this time.</li>
<li>Administer anti-D profilactically at 36-40 weeks gestation. It is advisable an <strong>indirect coombs</strong> test is done before administration to rule out sensitivity.</li>
<li>A great risk is associated with delivery process. Ensure anti-D is administered within 72 weeks after the birth of the baby. However it is advisable a <strong>direct coombs</strong> can be done before administration for confirm presence of maternal antibodies. A blood sample can be taken to confirm the rhesus factor of the newborn, if negative the mother carries no risk so administration of the anti D can be withdrawn.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="care-of-baby-after-birth">Care of baby after birth<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-baby-after-birth" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Continue monitoring the baby.</li>
<li>Blood works can be done to include:</li>
<li>hb level</li>
<li>bilirubin level</li>
<li>Rule out asphyxia neonatorum</li>
<li>Rule out kernicterus associated with high bilirubin levels.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Abortions</li>
<li>Miscarriages</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Jaundice</li>
<li>Birth asphyxia</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Infertility
&gt; Hydrops fetalis
&gt; IUFD
&gt; Still birth</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="premature-rupture-of-membranes">PREMATURE RUPTURE OF MEMBRANES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#premature-rupture-of-membranes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition: This is a condition occurring during pregnancy where there is rupture of the membrane at least 1 hour before onset of labour.</p>
<p>It can occur before at term and posses less risk to the fetus. If it occurs before 37 complete weeks of gestation it is called preterm premature rupture of membranes (PPROM).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Premature rupture of membranes (PROM)</li>
</ol>
<p>This is a condition occurring during pregnancy where there is rupture of the membrane at least 1 hour before onset of labour.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Preterm premature rupture of membranes (PPROM)</li>
</ol>
<p>Membranes have ruptured before 37 complete weeks gestation.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Prolonged premature rupture of membranes (Prolonged PROM)</li>
</ol>
<p>Membranes have ruptured and 24 hours have elapsed without onset of labour.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Pre-viable premature rupture of membranes (Pre-viable PROM)</li>
</ol>
<p>Membranes have ruptured when the baby can not survive once born.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-factors">Risk factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Infections</li>
</ul>

☑ previous history of prom
☑ Psychological problems

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Take proper history from mother</li>
<li>On speculum exam</li>
</ol>
<p>Fluid is seen coming from cervix or forming a pool in the posterior fornix</p>
<p>A gush of fluid after mother cough</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Nitrazine test</li>
</ol>
<p>Nitrazine paper or speculum blade attached to fluid color is yellow - blue alkalinity</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Ferning test</li>
</ol>
<p>Spread some fluid on a slide and let it dry on microscope amniotic fluid forms crystals</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Abdominal U/S reveals Oligohydromnous</li>
<li>Abdominal palpation reveals decreased fundal height</li>
<li>Do litmus test</li>
<li>Give a pad and later examine presence of amniotic fluid</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="differential-diagnosis">Differential diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#differential-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Urinary incontinence.</li>
<li>Sweating associated with pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<p>&gt; Normal vaginal discharge during pregnancy.
&gt; Increasing cervical discharge.
&gt; Semen.
&gt; Douch.
&gt; Loss of mucus plug.
&gt; Vesico- vaginal fistula.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit.</li>
<li>Reassure.</li>
<li>Provide adequate rest</li>
<li>Do a speculum to confirm a pool of fluid.</li>
<li>Avoid digital vaginal to decrease risk of infection.</li>
<li>Monitor FHR closely</li>
<li>Administer antibiotics to treat existing infection or profilactically.</li>
<li>If mother is below 37 weeks hospitalize.</li>
<li>Abdominal scan to assess fetal growth and complications of oligohydromnious e.g. hypoxia.</li>
<li>Do weekly RWBC to R/O infection</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>5</p>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>In case of signs of labour, administer drugs like salbutamol 4mg to prolong pregnancy.</li>
<li>Administer dexamethasone for lung maturity.</li>
<li>If membranes ruptured before 24 weeks, fetus is likely to succumb to problem of oligohydromnious or preterm birth: Termination of pregnancy is done</li>
<li>If pregnant more than 32 weeks gestation, fetus appears compromised e.g. hypoxia, intervene, labour is confirmed let it progress OR induce OR c/s</li>
<li>Monitor vital especially FHR</li>
<li>Observe amniotic fluid to R/o meconium</li>
<li>In case of infection or IUFD induction is done</li>
<li>Encourage personal hygiene i.e. change of pads</li>
<li>If prom happens after 37 weeks start the mother on antibiotics, manage for induction of labour and don't wait for spontaneous labour</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>antenatal profile</li>
<li>rest</li>
<li>management of condition e.g. pet, hypertension</li>
<li>early diagnosis and treatment of UTI</li>
<li>avoid smoking and illicit drugs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-to-the-mother">Complications to the mother<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-to-the-mother" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="to-the-fetus">To the fetus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#to-the-fetus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pre-eclampsia">PRE ECLAMPSIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pre-eclampsia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>It is a condition occurring during pregnancy &gt;20 weeks gestation characterized by high blood pressure and protein in urine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="aetiology">AETIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>It is associated with</p>
<ul>
<li>Toxicity produced by placenta for the first time</li>
<li>Over distension of the abdomen</li>
<li>Immunological changes as the fetus is developing</li>
</ul>
<p>The three events make the condition affect multi system and multi organ. The blood vessels become Leakey. Fluids now tend to shift from intravascular to extra vascular space.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing Factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Primigravida</li>
<li>Primipartenity</li>
<li>previous positive family or personal history of pet</li>
<li>Medical conditions e.g. diabetes, mellitus, hypertension, renal disease, URTI in advanced stage</li>
<li>elderly primigravida &gt;35 years</li>
<li>young primigravida &lt;18 years of age</li>
<li>Multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Hydatidiform mole</li>
<li>Hydropsfetalis</li>
<li>Polyhydromnious</li>
<li>Rhesus incompartity</li>
<li>Obese mothers</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification">Classification<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Mild pet - Pre-eclampsia without signs
Bp 140/90mmhg, protein ++ and gestation &gt;20 weeks</p>
<p>b) Severe pet - Pre-eclampsia with signs
Bp 160/110mmhg, protein +++ or blood pressure as for mild but with any sign of severity ad gestation &gt;20 weeks</p>
<p>c) Eclampsia
High blood pressure, protein in urine, gestation &gt;20 weeks and presence of fits.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="signs-of-severity-in-pet">Signs of severity in PET<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-of-severity-in-pet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>a) Sudden sharp rise in Bp
b) Diminished urinary output
c) Hypereflexia
d) Clonus
e) Blurred vision
f) Increase in proteinuria
g) Thrombocytopenia
h) Severe and persistent frontal headache
i) Nausea &amp; vomiting
j) Epigastric pain</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-pet-to-pregnancy">Effects of PET to pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-pet-to-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Placenta abruption</li>
<li>Intrauterine growth restriction</li>
<li>Prematurity</li>
<li>Intra uterine fetal hypoxia</li>
<li>Low birth weight</li>
<li>Damage to vital organs e.g. kidney, eye brain heart etc.</li>
<li>Intra uterine fetal death</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-pet-to-the-woman">Effects of PET to the woman<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-pet-to-the-woman" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>brain hypoxia</li>
<li>cerebral vascular accident</li>
<li>brain heriation</li>
<li>cerebral oedema</li>
<li>head injury</li>
<li>temporary blindness</li>
<li>pulmonary oedema</li>
<li>liver oedema</li>
<li>liver failure</li>
<li>liver rupture</li>
<li>kidney failure</li>
<li>HELLP syndrome</li>
</ol>
<p>NOTE: All women at risk of developing pet can receive aspirin throughout pregnancy to reduce the chances of developing pet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="d9d90b35">Mild pet – Pre eclampsia without signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d9d90b35" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is a condition occurring during pregnancy &gt;20 weeks gestation characterized by high blood pressure of 140/90mmgh and protein in urine ++.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-mild-pet">Management of mild PET<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-mild-pet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Note: All women at risk of developing pet should receive daily aspirin 150mgs. Research has shown that aspirin reduces the chances of developing pet.</p>
<p>a) Book the mother in high risk clinic
b) Schedule her on 2 weekly visits to the antenatal clinic
c) Take Bp and record
d) take weight and height
e) perform physical examination
f) Test urine for protein
g) Take fetal heart (between 120-160)
h) Measure the abdomen in order to detect abnormal fundal height.
i) Prescribe to the mother some mild sedatives e.g. phenobarbitone (30-60mg) to assist her acquire enough rest
j) Advice the mother on high protein diet
k) Advice the mother on rest at home</p>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>l) Advice the mother on fetal activity and any reduced activity she should come to the clinic. Reinforce this by teaching the mother on maintenance of fetal kick count (FKC) chart.</p>
<p>m) Advice the mother on signs of severe PET e.g. severe headache, epigastric pain. if she notices any she should come to the clinic.</p>
<p>n) Advice the mother to come for admission when pregnancy reaches 38 weeks gestation</p>
<p>o) Give the mother antihypertensive aldomet 250- 750mgs three times or twice a day and nifedipine 20 mgs twice a day.</p>
<p>p) Ensure the mother receives the other routine antenatal care services e.g.</p>
<ul>
<li>physical examination</li>
<li>provision of treated net</li>
<li>deworming</li>
<li>antenatal profile</li>
<li>administration of tetanus toxoid</li>
<li>administration of haematenics - IFAS</li>
<li>emtct</li>
<li>administration of sulfadoxine pymerathymine - sp</li>
<li>health education</li>
<li>book for next</li>
</ul>
<p>q) On the day the woman comes for next visit apart from routine ante natal care services ensure the following is done</p>
<ul>
<li>fetal heart rate monitoring to rule out fetal hypoxia</li>
<li>Fundal height measurement to rule out IUGR</li>
<li>Protein in urine</li>
<li>Blood pressure measurement</li>
<li>Drug compliance</li>
<li>Check signs of severity</li>
<li>FKC record</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fd188219">SEVERE PET – Pre-eclampsia with signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fd188219" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a condition occurring during pregnancy &gt;20 weeks gestation characterized by high blood pressure of 160/110mmgh and protein in urine +++.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-management">Principles of management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Control of blood pressure
b) Prevention of convulsions
c) delivery option</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-severe-pet">Management of severe PET<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-severe-pet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>a) Admit the mother in a quiet room in a facility capable to offer comprehensive emergency obstetrical and newborn care (if in a health centre refer)
b) Ensure mother gets enough bed rest with a 24 hour nursing coverage.
c) Reassure the mother
d) call for help from senior member present
e) Give the mother some sedatives e.g. phenobarbitone 30-60mg
f) The aim of management is to prevent convulsion, control Bp and prevent maternal and fetal death.
g) Management of blood pressure.</p>
<p>&gt; Administer intravenous hydralazine 5mgs as bolus slowly over 5 minutes. Repeat the dose every 30 minutes to a maximum of 20mgs. Aim at achieving a diastolic blood pressure of 90mmgh.
&gt; Once the diastolic is 90mmgh administer oral aldomet 250 - 750 mgs and nifedipine to prevent rebound high blood pressure.
&gt; Other drugs to include labetalol can be administered.</p>
<p>Example of how hydralazine administration,</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Time</th><th>Bp reading</th><th>dose</th><th>Remarks</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>10 am</td><td>160/120</td><td>5mgs</td><td>Check bp before next dose</td></tr><tr><td>10.30 am</td><td>150/110</td><td>5mgs</td><td>Monitor bp</td></tr><tr><td>11 00 am</td><td>140/90</td><td>Don’t give</td><td>Start oral antihypertensive. monitor bp</td></tr><tr><td>11.30 am</td><td>-</td><td>-</td><td>-</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Know how to prepare hydralazine and administer.</p>
<p>Step 1: Dilute hydralazine with 2 mls of water for injection.</p>
<p>Step 2: Use 20 mls syringe. Add 18 mls of the same diluent to the 2 mls to get a bigger volume of 20 ml.</p>
<p>Step 3: Divide 20 the mls into 4 parts. 5 mls is equal to 5 mgs.</p>
<p>step 4: Administer 5 mgs every 30 minutes until bp falls</p>
<p>h) prevention of fits</p>
<p>&gt; the drug of choice is magnesium sulphate - mgso4
&gt; comes in two concentrations 20% and 50%
&gt; administer loadig dose and maintenance dose
&gt; Loading dose - 4 gms of 20% intravenously slowly over 10 - 15 minutes plus 10gms of 50% deep intra muscularly (administer 5</p>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id=""><span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"></span></h1></div>
<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>gms on each buttock). Add 1- 2 mls of lignocain to each 5 gms (2 mls if you have 1% or 1 ml if administering 2% lignocain).</p>
<p>NOTE; in case you miss intravenous access administer only the 10gms of 50% intramuscularly as loading dose.</p>
<p>&gt; Maintenance dose – administer 5 gms of 50% mgso4 every 4 hours for 24 hrs. Or 1gm 20% mgso4 per hour intravenously of for 24 hours. Note- For the intravenous route ensure you use a pump.
&gt; In case the woman fits in the course of treatment administer as bolus 2 – 4gms of 20% mgso4 according to body weight (&lt;70 kgs give 2gms and &gt;70 kgs give 4 gms)</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-07fbb300.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<p>NOTE: in case of a fit while on mgso2, administer 2 – 4 gms as bolus of 20% 1.v. depending on the weight of the mother.</p>
<p>&lt; 70 kgs give 2gms. &gt;70 kgs give 4gms</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="how-to-convert-magnesium-sulphate-from-50-concentration-to-20-concentration">How to convert magnesium sulphate from 50% concentration to 20% concentration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-to-convert-magnesium-sulphate-from-50-concentration-to-20-concentration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Withdraw</th><th>concentration</th><th>Add water for injection OR normal saline</th><th>Current volume</th><th>Current concentration</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>8mls</td><td>4gms of 50%</td><td>12mls</td><td>20mls</td><td>20%mgso2</td></tr><tr><td>4mls</td><td>2gms of 50%</td><td>6mls</td><td>10mls</td><td>20%mgso2</td></tr><tr><td>2mls</td><td>1gms of 50%</td><td>3mls</td><td>5mls</td><td>20%mgso2</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>&gt; Put in place a mgso2 monitoring chart
&gt; Magnesium sulphate administration should be continued for 24 hours after
&gt; - Being started
&gt; - Delivery
&gt; OR
&gt; - fit/ convulsions
&gt; Monitor signs of magnesium toxicity which include
&gt; - diminished urinary output
&gt; - dark colored urine
&gt; - rapid pulse rate
&gt; - reduced respiratory rate &lt;16 breathe/min
&gt; - increased fetal heart rate
&gt; - positive clonus sign
&gt; - absence of deep tendon reflex – absence of patella reflex
&gt; In case of evidence of toxicity stop mgso4 and administer intravenous 1 gms of 10% calcium gluconate which is 10 mls slowly over 10 minutes.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260119-6368f57d.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg">
A health workers practice on each other on how to check for a deep tendon reflex.</p>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>i) fluid management</p>
<ul>
<li>Manage the woman dry to prevent complications.</li>
<li>Restrict fluid intake to 1ml/kg bwt/ hour OR 80mls per hour OR 1 ltr in 24 hours.</li>
<li>Strictly monitor input output. Retention of 1lts of fluids can be dangerous.</li>
</ul>
<p>j) Monitor blood pressure and fetal heart rate 4 hourly. Increase the frequency depending on the condition.
k) Fix a catheter to monitor/maintain input and output.
l) Advice the mother to take a balanced diet
m) Give the mother a fetal kick chart to monitor fetal movements and keep record as the fetus may die in the uterus.
n) Do daily weighing.
o) Advice the mother to maintain personal hygiene
p) Do daily abdominal palpation
q) Continue general care for antenatal mothers
r) investigations – carry out the following investigations</p>
<ul>
<li>grouping and cross-match</li>
<li>bilirubin level</li>
<li>liver enzymes</li>
<li>clotting time</li>
<li>clotting factors</li>
<li>hemoglobin level</li>
</ul>
<p>s) Perform a daily head to toe examination.
t) Observe signs of onset of labour and impending eclampsia.
u) If the condition is unstable aim at delivering the baby as fast as possible.
v) Mode of delivery will be determined by condition of the patient which may be induction of labour or ceaserian section</p>
<p>Management during induction</p>
<ul>
<li>Reassure the mother</li>
<li>Observe the general management of a mother on induction of labour</li>
<li>Strictly monitor input and output</li>
<li>Continue with administration of magnesium sulphate</li>
<li>Prepare resuscitative blood and equipments</li>
<li>Carry out the necessary investigations.</li>
<li>Rule out DIC</li>
<li>Prepare the delivery room which is supposed to be warm</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintain observations on the partograph to early detect maternal and fetal compromise.</li>
<li>When the mother progresses well and reaches 2nd stage give a generous episiotomy and if possible assisted vaginal delivery with vacuum extraction to fasten 2nd stage of labour.</li>
<li>After delivery syntocinon drip should run for at least 1 hour, to help effective uterine contraction to prevent primary post partum haemorrhage</li>
<li>Magnesium sulphate continued for the next 24 hours.</li>
<li>When the baby is born, after the immediate resuscitation in h/w refer the baby to baby care unit</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-during-peurperium">Management during peurperium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-peurperium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Puerperal pet is also common.</li>
<li>Provide specific and basic care during peurperium until discharge this include:-</li>
<li>Close observation of Bp</li>
<li>Continue with magnesium sulphate for the next 24 hours.</li>
<li>Nurse the mother in a quiet room</li>
<li>Maintain fluid input and output chart.</li>
<li>Test urine for protein daily</li>
<li>Maintain personal hygiene</li>
<li>Initiate breastfeeding early</li>
<li>Carry out 1st postnatal care services</li>
<li>If the mother improves discharge through MCH/FP for follow up</li>
<li>If the Bp is high discharge through medical outpatient clinic for follow up</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-severe-pet">Complications of severe PET<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-severe-pet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Eclampsia</li>
<li>Placenta abruption</li>
<li>Cerebral haemorrhage</li>
<li>Cerebral oedema</li>
<li>Cerebral hypoxia</li>
<li>Pulmonary oedema</li>
<li>Brain herniation</li>
<li>Acute renal failure</li>
<li>Intra uterine growth restriction</li>
<li>Intra uterine death</li>
<li>Neonatal death</li>
<li>Prematurity</li>
<li>Impaired liver function- HELLP syndrome</li>
<li>Visual disturbances to include temporary blindness.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="eclampsia">ECLAMPSIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#eclampsia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is a condition in pregnancy &gt;20 weeks gestation characterized by high blood pressure, protein in urine, and presence of fits.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="varieties">Varieties<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#varieties" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Anti-partum eclampsia – mother develops fits before onset of labour. This usually has 20% of the cases</li>
<li>Intra-partum eclampsia – mother fitting with onset of labour. This usually has 45% of the cases</li>
<li>Post-partum eclampsia – fits take place after delivery of the baby within 1st 24 hours. Usually prevalence is almost 35% of all cases.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="aetiology">AETIOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aetiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The onset is almost sudden with very high blood pressure especially the diastolic</p>
<ul>
<li>In rare occasions eclampsia may occur in the absence of warning signs.</li>
<li>These include:-
a) Nausea and vomiting
b) Blurred vision
c) Severe frontal headache
d) epigastric pain
e) drownness
f) sharp rising blood pressure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-an-eclamptic-fit">STAGES OF AN ECLAMPTIC FIT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-an-eclamptic-fit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The eclamptic fit is classified into 4 stages</p>
<p>a) Premonitory stage
b) Tonic stage
c) Chlonic stage
d) Coma</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="premonitory-stage">Premonitory stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#premonitory-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>It lasts about 10-20 seconds and patient may fall unconscious, rolls her eyes and the head drawn on one side and may have twitching of the muscles of the face and hands.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tonic-stage">Tonic stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tonic-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Lasts about 10-20 seconds, muscles go into spasm and become rigid, the teeth and fists are clenched, eyes staring in one direction and the feet are inverted with the toes flexed and the patient gets respiratory arrest.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chronic-stage">Chronic stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chronic-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It last for about 60-90 seconds, muscles relax and contract alternatively. There is great jerking movements and the patient may be thrown out of bed if not protected and taken care of. The alternate opening and closing of the jaws may make the patient bite the tongue. There is increased frothy saliva which may be blood stained indicating trauma to the tongue.</p>
<p>The face is congested and horrible distorted, breathing will be noisy and forceful. Convulsions will subside gradually.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="coma">Coma<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#coma" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Patient soon goes into coma or deep sleep, she becomes deeply unconscious and breathing continues to be noisy and rapid.</li>
<li>Coma stage may be followed by one or two fits before the patients recovers.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="differential-diagnosis">Differential diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#differential-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral malaria</li>
<li>Epilepsy</li>
<li>Meningitis</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-eclamptic-fit-to-the-pregnancy">Effects of eclamptic fit to the pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-eclamptic-fit-to-the-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Placental abruption</li>
<li>Onset of labour</li>
<li>Intra uterine fetal hypoxia</li>
<li>Intrauterine fetal death</li>
<li>Post partum haemorrhage</li>
</ol>

<p>studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-during-a-fit">Management during a fit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-a-fit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Call for help</li>
<li>Reassure relatives</li>
<li>Ensure clear airway</li>
<li>Do not leave woman alone</li>
<li>Guard the mother to protect her from injury and remove harmful objects near her</li>
<li>Do not restrain the mother.</li>
<li>Ensure privacy</li>
<li>Turn the mother's head on one side for drainage of saliva and suction</li>
<li>Administer oxygen if necessary by facemask</li>
<li>Start the woman on magnesium sulphate, MgSO₄, dosage as for severe pet.</li>
<li>Monitor for signs of magnesium toxicity.</li>
<li>If the woman is on magnesium sulphate and is still convulsing administer diazepam. Start with 5mgs slowly as a bolus up to 10 mgs and closely monitor maternal respiratory rate. Do not withhold mgso4 administration.</li>
<li>Control administration of fluids. <strong>Manage the woman dry.</strong></li>
<li>Record frequency, duration and parts affected by convulsions</li>
<li>Delivery of the baby should be within <strong>12 hours maximum.</strong></li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="if-in-a-health-centre">If in a health centre<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-in-a-health-centre" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Transfer the patient in a hospital after sedating heavily</li>
<li>Carry with you oxygen, delivery pack containing sterile gloves, forceps, mouth guard, syringes and needles, patients notes and record</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="if-in-a-hospital">If in a hospital<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-in-a-hospital" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Aim at delivery the fetus as quickly as possible since the fetus is already in great danger. Do not take more than 12 hours before the baby is delivered with whatever option.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prepare a quiet room with all resuscitative drugs and equipment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Position the patient with the head tilted on one side and maintain a clear airway</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sanction the mouth if necessary</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer hydralazine to control Bp</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administer MgSO₄ as prescribed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give antibiotics prolaphylactical e.g. ampicillin 500mgs QID</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The mother might be into labour spontaneously following the fits, if not induction of labour is commenced assisted by vacuum extraction during 2nd stage.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Have an indwelling catheter in situ (in place)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continue checking vital signs including Bp and fetal heart rate if baby is still alive.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Perform physical examination to assess improvement of oedema</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Continue maintaining personal hygiene to prevent infection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When labour progress well &amp; baby us delivered receive baby in warm room and after the initial resuscitation in labour ward transfer baby to baby care unit for further management.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-after-delivery">Management after delivery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-after-delivery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Continue with magnesium sulphate dose.</li>
<li>Monitor Bp closely</li>
<li>Maintain heavy sedation for the first 48 hours</li>
<li>Nurse in a quiet room to prevent occurrence of another fit</li>
<li>Maintain input, output chart to assess improvement of kidneys</li>
<li>maintain personal hygiene.</li>
<li>Offer the other routine post natal care services.</li>
<li>In case of impaired vision or temporary blindness reassure the mother.</li>
<li>When condition improves discharge through MCH/FP clinic but when Bp persists to be high discharge through medical outpatient clinic for follow up.</li>
<li>Note in the discharge summary that the mother had eclampsia.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Cerebral haemorrhage</li>
<li>Cerebral hypoxia</li>
<li>Cerebral oedema</li>
<li>Acute renal failure</li>
<li>Liver damage</li>
<li>Pulmonary oedema</li>
<li>Inhalation pneumonia</li>
<li>Congenital cardiac failure</li>
<li>Permanent hypertension</li>
<li>head injury</li>
<li>Still birth</li>
<li>Neonatal death</li>
<li>maternal death</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="ante-partum-haemorrhage-aph">ANTE-PARTUM HAEMORRHAGE - APH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ante-partum-haemorrhage-aph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Definition - This is bleeding from the birth canal during pregnancy after 20th week of gestation and before labour.</p>
<p>This places the life of mother and the fetus at great risk.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-on-fetus">Effects on Fetus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-on-fetus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>(i) Fetal compromise
(ii) Still birth
(iii) neonatal death</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-on-mother">Effects on mother<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-on-mother" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>(i) Shock
(ii) Anaemia
(iii) Disseminated Intravascular Coagulation
(iv) Increased risk to ceaserian section
(v) Maternal death</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a) Any conditions increasing blood pressure e.g. PET
b) Following external cephalic version
c) Trauma
d) Polyhydrominous
e) Anaemia especially folic acid deficiency
f) Multiparity
g) Infection
h) Shock
i) Ruptured uterus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classifications-of-aph">Classifications of APH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classifications-of-aph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>j) Extra placental bleeding – This is the bleeding from the sides and not on the placental surface (bleeding not associated with placenta)
ii) Placental bleeding – It is the bleeding from the placental surface i.e. due to placenta previa or abruption</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-aph-mild">Management of APH (MILD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-aph-mild" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Admit mother in a quiet room and provide complete bed rest.</li>
<li>Provide mother with pads and preserve all soaked pads for doctors assessment</li>
<li>At about 37 weeks gestation do surfactant test to confirm lung maturity of the unborn baby</li>
<li>Take blood for extra and Hb level</li>
<li>!administer sedatives e.g. phenorbarbitone to enhance complete rest and relaxation</li>
<li>Maintain nutritional status by giving a diet rich in proteins, iron plenty of vitamins, carbohydrates and fluids</li>
<li>Maintain personal hygiene by performing a daily bed birth, vulva toilet &amp; treat pressure areas</li>
<li>Do T,P,R and Bp <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mfrac><mn>1</mn><mn>4</mn></mfrac></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\frac{1}{4}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1.1901em; vertical-align: -0.345em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mopen nulldelimiter"></span><span class="mfrac"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8451em;"><span style="top: -2.655em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">4</span></span></span></span><span style="top: -3.23em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="frac-line" style="border-bottom-width: 0.04em;"></span></span><span style="top: -3.394em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 3em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">1</span></span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.345em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mclose nulldelimiter"></span></span></span></span></span></span> hourly</li>
<li>Prepare to receive the newborn i.e.
(i) Prepare resuscitative drugs and equipment
(ii) A warm room or incubator
(iii) After resuscitation refer to baby care unit for further management</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-severe-aph">Management of severe APH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-severe-aph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Resuscitate the mother if she is I shock</li>
<li>Take blood GXM and order blood Hb level</li>
<li>Set up an intravenous infusion as soon as possible to treat shock</li>
<li>Give sedatives or analgesics if necessary</li>
<li>Administer oxygen by mask to increase oxygen concentration both the maternal and fetal circulation</li>
<li>Insert an indwelling catheter to monitor the woman's output</li>
<li>If its in a dispensary, refer mother to a hospital</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="placenta-pravia">PLACENTA PRAVIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#placenta-pravia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is bleeding from separation of a placenta that is partially or wholly implanted in the lower uterine segment.</p>
<p>It places mother and fetus at high risk and leads to obstetric emergency.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="degrees-of-placenta-previa">Degrees of placenta previa<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#degrees-of-placenta-previa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Type 1 - 1st degree</p>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>The majority of the placenta is on the upper segment. Part of the placenta is on the lower uterine margin. Also referred to as lateral placenta previa.</li>
<li>Blood loss is usually mild and the mother and fetus are in good condition</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="type-2-2nd-degree">Type 2 - 2nd degree<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#type-2-2nd-degree" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The placenta is partially located in the lower segment near the internal cervical OS. Also referred to as marginal placenta preavia.</li>
<li>Blood loss moderate although maternal and fetal condition can vary. Fetal hypoxia is more likely to present than maternal shock</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="type-3-3rd-degree">Type 3 - 3rd degree<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#type-3-3rd-degree" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The placenta is located over the internal cervical OS but not centrally.</li>
<li>It is also referred to as complete placenta praevia.</li>
<li>Bleeding is likely to be severe in late pregnancy and vaginal delivery is impossible because the placenta precedes the fetus</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="type-4-4th-degree">Type 4 - 4th degree<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#type-4-4th-degree" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Placenta is located centrally over the internal cervical OS. Also referred to as total placenta praevia.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors-to-placenta-praevia">Predisposing factors to placenta praevia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-to-placenta-praevia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-multiparity">1. Multiparity.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-multiparity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is as a result of the fertilized ovum searching of a new site for implantation. the mare the number previous pregnancies the higher the risk of the present pregnancy taking place at the lower uterine segment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-multiple-pregnancy">2. Multiple pregnancy.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-multiple-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In this case the pregnancy is carrying more than one fetus. Two scenarios may contribute to the placenta appearing on the lower uterine segment. The size of the placenta may be bigger OR the each fetus may be having its own placenta. This increases the chances of the placenta utilizing the lower uterine segment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-abnormalities-of-placenta-e-g-bi-patitte">3. Abnormalities of placenta e.g. bi-patitte<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-abnormalities-of-placenta-e-g-bi-patitte" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>A placental abnormality like placenta bi- patitte where the placenta is split to two or three as in placenta tri- patitte the one part may attach on the lower uterine segment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-presence-of-fibroids">4. Presence of fibroids<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-presence-of-fibroids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The area within the uterus where a fibroid is present may not offer a good site for implantation. If the fibroid is fundal there are higher chances for the placenta to be previa. The more the fibroids et higher the risk.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-previous-history-of-surgery">5. Previous history of surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-previous-history-of-surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In case the woman had any surgery that involved the uterus e.g. myomectomy, ceaserian section e.t.c. the site heals with formation of fibrous tissue. This may discourage implantation leading to placenta previa if the incision is fundal. If it so happens that placenta still attaches itself to a place like this the risk of retained placenta develops.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-age-especially-under-20-uterus-not-well-developed">6. Age especially under 20 uterus not well developed<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-age-especially-under-20-uterus-not-well-developed" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The uterine cavity is not well developed. This increases the chances of the uterus encroaching the lower segment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-smoking">7. Smoking<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-smoking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Smoking predisposes the body to many conditions placenta previa being among them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features-of-placenta-praevia">Clinical features of placenta praevia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-of-placenta-praevia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Bleeding is painless</li>
<li>Bleeding usually occurs at rest or sleep</li>
<li>Onset is gradual.</li>
<li>Blood is bright red in colour</li>
<li>Blood flows with a trickle</li>
<li>Positive history of intermittent bleeding during pregnancy</li>
<li>Abdomen not tender on palpation.</li>
<li>Presenting part is high</li>
<li>Malpresentation are common i.e. Oblique</li>
<li>Fetal parts easily palpable.</li>
<li>FHR is usually present</li>
<li>Lower uterine pole feels empty OR a soft mass can be felt on palpation.</li>
<li>The amount of blood loss corresponds to mother's condition.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Clinical features</li>
<li>Abdominal scan</li>
<li>Speculum examination</li>
</ul>
