<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-placenta-praevia">Management of placenta praevia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-placenta-praevia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Management will depend on the following:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amount of blood loss</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maturity of fetus</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Condition of mother and fetus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Stage of pregnancy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Admit the mother and offer complete bed rest until bleeding stops</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>if in a health facility that cannot offer emergency obstetrical and newborn care refer the woman to such a facility.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>3 days after bleeding stops do speculum examination after bleeding stops to rule out accidental causes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Check the Hb level of the mother</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Placental function is monitored by means of fetal kick chart and antenatal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ultra sound and scans are done to observe the position of the placenta in relation to the cervical OS as the lower segment grows.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>NOTE</strong>: Majority of placentas that were on the lower uterine segment usually migrate by 28 week of gestation.</p>
<ul>
<li>in case the pregnancy is going to be discontinued preterm consider administering steroids to the mother, dethamethasone to ensure lung maturity.</li>
<li>if the mother is rhesus negative ad you suspect rhesus iso-immunization, the woman should receive rhesus immune globulins. Not unless it is confirmed the husband is rhesus negative.</li>
<li>Closely monitor fetal well being.</li>
<li>Blood should be taken for full count, cross matching and clothing studies</li>
<li>An intravenous infusion should be in progress and several units of blood may be transfused with woman's consent</li>
<li>An anaesthetist will be present in helping the woman to make a decision on use of general or regional anesthesia</li>
<li>Midwife should comfort and encourage the mother since she may feel anxious in preparation for theatre</li>
<li>Patient should be mentally and physically support.</li>
<li>After delivery of the baby amstl to prevent pph</li>
<li>Mother should be given prophylactic antibiotics.</li>
<li>Start the woman on haematenics</li>
<li>Record on her mother booklet that she had aph.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complication-of-placenta-praevia">Complication of placenta praevia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complication-of-placenta-praevia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Haemorrhage</li>
<li>Anesthetic and surgical complications</li>
<li>intra uterine fetal growth restriction.</li>
<li>Retained placenta</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Placenta accrete</li>
<li>Air embolism</li>
<li>Fetal hypoxia</li>
<li>Fetal death</li>
<li>Maternal death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="placenta-abruption">PLACENTA ABRUPTION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#placenta-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is bleeding during pregnancy due to premature separation of a normally situated placenta occurring after 20th week of pregnancy and prior to 3rd stage of labour.</p>
<p>It is characterized by formation of retro-placental clot</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="predisposing-factors-to-placenta-abruption">Predisposing factors to placenta abruption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-to-placenta-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Trauma</li>
<li>Obstetrical manovours</li>
<li>Uterine massage</li>
<li>Drugs</li>
<li>Short cord</li>
<li>Polyhydrominous</li>
<li>Severe anaemia</li>
<li>Pet</li>
<li>Cardiac disease</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Renal disease</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-placenta-abruption">Types of placenta abruption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-placenta-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>i) Revealed accidental haemorrhage</p>
<ul>
<li>Its most common</li>
<li>Blood escape through uterus the cervix and vagina</li>
<li>Bleeding may be slight or severe</li>
<li>There is low urine output with proteinuria</li>
</ul>
<p>ii) Concealed accidental haemorrhage</p>
<ul>
<li>Most severe but least common</li>
<li>No vagina bleeding</li>
<li>Formation of retro-placental clot between the uterine walls and placenta</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>iii) Combined accidental haemorrhage</p>
<ul>
<li>Presence of both revealed or concealed haemorrhage</li>
<li>The patient may be in shock</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clinical-features-of-placental-abruption">Clinical features of placental abruption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-of-placental-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Amount of bleeding may not equal to mothers condition.</li>
<li>Bleeding accompanied with pain.</li>
<li>Patient looks ill and anxious</li>
<li>Mother is in shock i.e. weak pulse</li>
<li>Abdomen tender on palpation and guarding.</li>
<li>Fetal parts are difficult to palpate</li>
<li>Fetal heart sounds are absent in severe cases</li>
<li>There might be history of trauma or fall</li>
<li>Low urine output</li>
<li>Raised fundal height</li>
<li>Blood is dark red with clots</li>
<li>Bleeding is in gushes</li>
<li>Mother may be edematous</li>
<li>Malpresentation is not common.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-placenta-abruption">Management of placenta abruption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-placenta-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If in a health centre refer mother to hospital</li>
<li>Start on intravenous therapy prior to transfusion</li>
<li>Admit mother in a delivery site</li>
<li>This is an obstetric emergency.</li>
<li>Prepare the mother for emergency ceaserian section.</li>
<li>Midwife should comfort and encourage the mother by attending to her needs</li>
<li>Give a suitable analgesic e.g. pethidine 100-150mg to alleviate pain</li>
<li>Give plasma expanders if blood is not ready for transfusion</li>
<li>The woman should lie on her side in order to prevent vena cava and compression by the gravid status.</li>
<li>If bleeding is much, or in shock resuscitate by rapid collection of hypovolaemia</li>
<li>Take vital signs ¼ hourly</li>
<li>Insert an indwelling catheter to assess urinary output</li>
<li>Urine should be tested for protein</li>
<li>Record fluid intake accurately</li>
<li>If bleeding continues and comprised fetal heart rate is present, caesarian section may be required</li>
<li>Midwife should give the woman psychological support because of her shocked</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Rupture of membranes is beneficial as can assist in minimizing haemorrhage. In case this is done the woman can be started on oxytocin infusion to hasten labour.</li>
<li>Perform a speculum examination if bleeding is from uterus</li>
<li>Continue with abdominal palpations transfuse mother</li>
<li>Prepare to do resuscitation for the asphyxiated baby and transfer the baby to baby care unit. I case the baby is not alive counsel the mother to expect a dead fetus.</li>
<li>Assess cervical dilation if mother is in labour and deliver baby if condition allows</li>
<li>Examination under anesthesia is done in theatre</li>
<li>Check blood clotting time.</li>
<li>In case of blood clotting disorders then consider managing also as a case of DIC.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="complications-of-placenta-abruption">Complications of placenta abruption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications-of-placenta-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Blood coagulatory disorder</li>
<li>PPH</li>
<li>Acute renal failure</li>
<li>Anterior pituitary necrosis/shehaan,s syndrome</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Puerperal sepsis</li>
<li>Amniotic fluid embolism</li>
<li>Intra uterine fetal hypoxia</li>
<li>Intra uterine fetal growth restriction</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="similarities-of-placenta-praevia-and-abruption">Similarities of placenta praevia and abruption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#similarities-of-placenta-praevia-and-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Both affect the placenta</li>
<li>both appear after 20th week gestation</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-differences-between-placenta-praevia-and-placenta-abruption">Characteristics differences between placenta praevia and placenta abruption<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-differences-between-placenta-praevia-and-placenta-abruption" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Placenta praevia</th><th>Placenta abruption</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Bleeding is form placental site due to premature separation of the placenta which lies wholly or partly lies in lower uterine segment</td><td>Bleeding from early separation of placenta which lies normally in the fundus.</td></tr><tr><td>Painless.</td><td>Painful</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Can even at occur at rest or asleep</th><th>Can be positive history of trauma or fall</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Positive history intermittent bleeding</td><td>No history of intermittent bleeding</td></tr><tr><td>Blood is bright red</td><td>Blood is dark red</td></tr><tr><td>Bleeding may be continuous and in a trickle</td><td>Bleeding may be in gashes</td></tr><tr><td>No signs of pre-eclampsia may be present</td><td>Signs of pre-eclampsia may be present</td></tr><tr><td>Fetus may be alive</td><td>Fetus is usually dead</td></tr><tr><td>Uterus is soft and non tender</td><td>Uterus is hard and tender and guarding</td></tr><tr><td>Fetal parts are easily palpable</td><td>Fetal parts are not palpable</td></tr><tr><td>Uterine size correspond to gestation</td><td>Uterine size may be larger does not correspond to gestation.</td></tr><tr><td>Urinary output is normal</td><td>Urinary output is low</td></tr><tr><td>Fetal movements are normal</td><td>Fetal movements decreases</td></tr><tr><td>All bleeding seen</td><td>May be concealed</td></tr><tr><td>FHR can easily be heard if alive</td><td>FHR not easily heard if alive</td></tr><tr><td>Presenting part is high</td><td>Presenting part may be engaged</td></tr><tr><td>Blood loss equals to mothers condition</td><td>Blood loss may not be equals mothers condition</td></tr><tr><td>Malpresentation are common</td><td>Malpresentations not common.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-management-of-aph">General management of APH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-management-of-aph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If in a health centre always refer all pregnant women bleeding to the hospital</li>
<li>Ensure there is running IV fluid of saline before transferring the patient</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>A health worker should accompany the woman to the hospital</li>
<li>Always admit the patient even if bleeding is not apparent or severe</li>
<li>Take careful history, any associated pain, history of bleeding earlier in pregnancy or history of trauma</li>
<li>Note the amount and character of bleeding.</li>
<li>The specific management will depend on</li>
<li>Onset of spontaneous labour</li>
<li>Condition of the fetus</li>
<li>Cause of APH and severity</li>
<li>Gestation</li>
<li>If the bleeding is continuous or not</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-mild-aph">Management of mild APH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-mild-aph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit patient in the ward</li>
<li>Provide complete bed rest and observe her closely</li>
<li>Prepare and assist in taking investigation in view to prolonged pregnancy e.g. blood group and cross match</li>
<li>Do a speculum examination</li>
<li>Preserve soiled pads for assessment</li>
<li>Order a placentography (x-ray to visual placental position</li>
<li>Before 37 weeks gestation you can do a surfactant test to confirm fetal lung maturity</li>
<li>Prepare the patient for examination under anesthesia</li>
<li>Administer drugs e.g. sedatives phenobarbitone 30-60 mgs to ensure complete rest and relaxation</li>
<li>Maintain nutritional status of the mother by giving a diet rich in protein, iron, vitamins and fluids</li>
<li>Maintain hygiene by performing bed bath daily</li>
<li>Mouth wash 6 hours</li>
<li>Vulva toiled PRN and treat pressure areas</li>
<li>Take vital signs observations and report any abnormality</li>
<li>The doctor will determine mode of delivery.</li>
<li>During delivery prepare to receive the new bon that is;
a) Resuscitate drugs and equipments
b) A warm room
c) An incubator ready
d) Inform newborn care unit just in case you might need to refer the newborn for further management.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-severe-aph">Management of severe APH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-severe-aph" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Admit the mother</li>
<li>Call for help</li>
<li>Inform other departments</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>reassure the mother and relatives</li>
<li>Prepare for resuscitation.</li>
<li>Prepare an observation tray</li>
<li>Ensure a clear airway and give oxygen by mask</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs and FHR ¼ hourly</li>
<li>Keep the patient warm</li>
<li>Take blood for grouping and cross match and transfuse patient</li>
<li>Start IV fluids, N/S</li>
<li>Put in indwelling or self retaining catheter</li>
<li>Monitor input output by maintaining a correct fluid chart</li>
<li>Test urine for albumin, acetone and sugar</li>
<li>If the patient is for examination and anesthesia and possible caesarian section prepare her.</li>
<li>Prepare her for emergency caesarian section or hysterectomy.</li>
<li>Prepare to receive an asphyxiated baby.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="maternal-complications">Maternal complications.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#maternal-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Shock</li>
<li>Renal failure</li>
<li>Sheehan’s syndrome</li>
<li>Coagulation disorders</li>
<li>Anaemia</li>
<li>Sepsis</li>
<li>maternal death</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="baby">Baby<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#baby" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>Intra uterine growth restriction</li>
<li>Prematurity</li>
<li>Fetal hypoxia</li>
<li>Intra uterine fetal death</li>
<li>Asphyxia neonatorum</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="twin-pregnancy">TWIN PREGNANCY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#twin-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Definition:</strong> This is when there is presence of more than one fetus in the uterus</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">Causes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cause is unknown.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors-women-at-risk">Predisposing factors/women at risk<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors-women-at-risk" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol>
<li>Personal history</li>
<li>Family history</li>
<li>Multiparity</li>
<li>People who used fertility drugs</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="presentation">Presentation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presentation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Cephalic/ Breech presentation</li>
<li>Breech/cephalic presentation</li>
<li>Cephalic/cephalic presentation</li>
<li>Breech/breech presentation</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>On physical examination</p>
<p>a) Inspection- Over distended abdomen</p>
<ul>
<li>Abdomen is oval and not global</li>
<li>Visibility of multiple fetal movements of the abdomen at term</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Palpation- Multiple fetal poles</p>
<ul>
<li>Higher fundal height as compared to gestation</li>
<li>Multiple fetal parts are palpation</li>
<li>1st palpation of fundal height above the umbilicus after delivery of 1st twin, query and diagnose 2 twin</li>
<li>Reduce fetal head side compared to gestation age</li>
</ul>
<p>c) Auscultation- follow rule of 10.</p>
<ul>
<li>2 fetal heart rate distance of 10cm a part and taken the same time at difference 10 beats per min</li>
</ul>
<p>d) Investigations- increased level of H.C.G hormone query multiple pregnancy</p>
<ul>
<li>Increased level of AFP &lt; Apha fetal protein present in the body of human being during pregnancy fetal congenital abnormalities</li>
</ul>
<p>e) History - Personal history of previous multiple pregnancies</p>
<ul>
<li>Family history of previous multiple pregnancies</li>
<li>History of exaggerated pressure symptoms</li>
<li>History of exaggerated minor disorders</li>
</ul>
<p>f) Radiography - Demonstration of two amniotic sacs from the eight week of gestation</p>
<ul>
<li>Visibility of more than one twin in the uterus on the 12th week (U/LS)</li>
<li>Visibility of more than one skeleton by X-ray from the 16th week</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="monozygotic">Monozygotic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monozygotic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Are babies as a result of fertilization of one sperm one ovum.</p>
<p>Separation to form 2 babies occur very early during embryology.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="characteristics">Characteristics<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Same physical characteristics</li>
<li>Same mental characteristics</li>
<li>Same blood group</li>
<li>Same sex</li>
<li>Share fetal circulation</li>
<li>Share same amniotic sac</li>
<li>The same figure prints</li>
<li>Very prone to congenital abnormalities</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="dzygotic">Dzygotic<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dzygotic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Result from fertilization of different ovam with different sperms</p>
<ol>
<li>Different physical characteristics</li>
<li>Different or same metal characteristics</li>
<li>Same sex or different sex</li>
<li>Same or different blood groups</li>
<li>Do not share the same circulations</li>
<li>Do not share the amniotic sac</li>
<li>Lower risk to congenital abnormalities</li>
<li>Different ova different sperm</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-during-second-stage">Management during second stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-second-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="delivery-of-the-first-twin">Delivery of the first twin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#delivery-of-the-first-twin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Perform ve and confirm the presentation, raptures membranes if not raptured</li>
<li>If presentation cephalic support the perineum and encourage the mother to push with every contraction</li>
<li>Raise the heed slightly and clear the air way and check for cord around the neck</li>
<li>Allow the baby to restitute</li>
<li>Hold the baby's head by the temporal and do a downward fraction to deliver the anterior shoulder up to the mid upper arm, then upward fraction to deliver posterior shoulder up to the mid arm.</li>
<li>Deliver the baby by lateral flexion onto the mother's abdomen</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Wipe the baby, clear airway, clamp and cut the cord and show the sex of the baby to the mother and hand over the baby to the assistance for immediate management which include,</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Keep the baby warm</li>
<li>Administer vitamin K</li>
<li>Administer tetracycline</li>
<li>If the mother PMTC is R, give nevirapine depending unto the weight of the baby</li>
<li>Score the baby at 5 and 10 minutes, back to breastfeed</li>
<li>Label the baby as first twin and inspect</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>NOTE: Withhold administration of syntocinon</strong></p>
<p><strong>Delivery of second twin</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Palpate the mother's abdomen to confirm second twin. The fundus will be above the umbilicus.
Also palpate to confirm the lie and presentation if in transverse perform external cephalic version, rotate the baby follow its face until engagement take place.</li>
<li>Do V.E, rapture the membranes,</li>
<li>In case contractions have done down administer 5 I.U cyntocinon IV in 500ml pf NIS to run 10 drops per minute.</li>
<li>Deliver the baby using the normal procedure as mentioned above.</li>
<li>Label as second twin.</li>
<li>In case the fetus is in transverse lie perform either podalic or cephalic version.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Podallic version</strong></p>
<p>Insert your hand inside the vagina canal unto the uterus get hold of the fetal legs by the pedals. Pull down the legs and deliver baby as breech. Wipe the baby, clamp and cut the cord and hand over the assistant follow the above procedure and label as second twin.</p>
<p><strong>Cephalic version</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>One hand applies traction on the fetal head abdominally through the occiput directing it into the pelvis.</li>
<li>The other hand applies an upward traction of the buttocks to position them at the fundus. Baby if born cephalic.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="third-stage-of-labour">Third stage of labour<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#third-stage-of-labour" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<li>Palpate to rule out another twin, if not administer 10 I.U cyntocinon and deliver the placental at once with (CCT) controlled cord traction (amstl).</li>
<li>Start 20 I.U cyntocinon IV on 500ml normal saline to run for one hour.
prophylactic management of pph</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="peurperium">Peurperium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#peurperium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Thorough first examination of the baby should be done to rule out congenital abnormalities.</li>
<li>Just like for any other mother.</li>
<li>Strengthen family planning education</li>
<li>Counsel on parenting</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="essential-hypertension">Essential hypertension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#essential-hypertension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is where there is elevation of blood pressure over 140/90 mmhg present in two or more occasions prior to 20 week gestation which is not due to pathogenically condition e.g. renal disease like chronic nephritis.</p>
<p>NB- essential hypertension should not be confused with high BP in PET as PET usually occurs after 20 week of gestation accompanied by protein in urine.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="atielogy">ATIELOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#atielogy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>80 % of the essential hypertension cases will give a positive history personal history or family history of hypertension.</p>
<p>Other causes could be stress situations e.g. divorce, or unwanted pregnancy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="parthophysiology">Parthophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parthophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>High blood pressure can lead to mother developing PET with all its signs and symptoms.</li>
<li>May lead to cerebral haemorrhage causing vascular accidents which can cause death to the mother.</li>
<li>It may affect the life of the fetus in the uterus and the fetus may be born as a light for dates.</li>
<li>This may also cause placental abruption.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="predisposing-factors">Predisposing factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#predisposing-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Family history of hypertension</li>
<li>Any history of toxaemia in the previous pregnancies.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-essential-hypertension-to-the-pregnancy">Effects of essential hypertension to the pregnancy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-essential-hypertension-to-the-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Increased maternal morbidity e.g. placental abruption, PET.</li>
<li>High BP may cause acute renal failure leading to oliguria and final coma.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="to-the-fetus">To the fetus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#to-the-fetus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Intra uterine growth retardation.</li>
<li>Intra uterine fetal death</li>
<li>Prematurity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="affects-of-pregnancy-on-essential-hypertension">Affects of pregnancy on essential hypertension.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#affects-of-pregnancy-on-essential-hypertension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The blood pressure may increase during pregnancy and after 20 weeks and signs of PET may appear.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objective">Objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Is to control the blood pressure and prevent PET from occurring.</li>
<li>To obtain a good supply of oxygen to the fetus especially during placental formation period.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="note">Note:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#note" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>If the fetus fails to grow adequately and the mother's condition deteriorates induction of labour can be done even before term.</p>
<p>Management will depend on the severity of the essential hypertension.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-mild-essential-hypertension">Management of mild essential hypertension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-mild-essential-hypertension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this category the blood pressure is usually not above 150/90. If this body is recorded during the antenatal visit the midwife should refer the mother to the obstetrician for evaluation and investigation.</p>
<p>The mother can be managed as an outpatient for it is possible for her to get enough r3est at home. This can be achieved with administration of a mild sedative to make her rest and allay anxiety. She should attend weeks ANC clinic.</p>
<p>During each visit the mother should be monitored blood pressure and physical examination done.</p>
<p>Advice the mother on diet i.e. high protein and low fat and salt.</p>
<p>Advice the mother on fetal kick count at home</p>
<p>Can report to the clinic in case of any abnormality e.g. reduced fetal movements.</p>
<p>Weekly investigations of urine for urinalysis, culture and sensitivity, renal function, blood for urea and electrolyte can be done</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-of-severe-hypertension">Management of severe hypertension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-severe-hypertension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Admit the mother I the antenatal room in quiet place.</p>
<p>Reassure the mother</p>
<p>Observe vital signs 4 hourly</p>
<p>Provide a balanced diet high in protein with low sodium</p>
<p>Weigh the mother daily</p>
<p>Do physical examination daily to rule out oedema and IUGR</p>
<p>Monitor input and output</p>
<p>Put the mother on drugs e.g. antihypertensive</p>
<p>Encourage rest</p>
<p>Continue with general nursing care</p>
<p>Do surfactant test at 36- 37 weeks to confirm fetal lung maturity and with apposite test6 the mother can be prescribed induction of labour.</p>
<p>Prepare to receive a baby with a poor score.</p>
<p>Assist second stage with a generous episiotomy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-during-puerperium">Management during puerperium<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-during-puerperium" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>☑ Continue 4 hourly observation especially BP.
☑ Continue with daily physical examination and assess for oedema.
☑ Ct with sedatives for rest.
☑ Ct a balanced diet.
☑ Maintain good personal h7ygiene.
☑ Keep the baby warm.
☑ Ct with general care of a mother in puerperium.
☑ If the condition improves discharge the mother through MCH/FP and if the high BP persists through medical clinic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complications">Complications<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="malaria-in-pregnancy-mip">MALARIA IN PREGNANCY - MIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#malaria-in-pregnancy-mip" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is a parasitic infection of the genus plasmodium which is spread by mosquito. The plasmodium species responsible is plasmodium falciparum.</p>
<p>It is one of the diseases of public health interest on Kenya.</p>
<p>It is a major cause of maternal morbidity and mortality accounting to 10% of maternal deaths.</p>
<p>By preventing malaria in pregnancy will save approximately 25000 lives each year.</p>
<p>Pregnant women who are at higher risk of contacting malaria</p>
<p>I. Women in their 1st and 2nd trimester
II. HIV infected
III. Visitors from no or low malaria zone</p>
<p>Kenya has 4 malaria epidemiological zones:</p>
<ol>
<li>Endemic</li>
<li>Seasonal transmission</li>
<li>Epidemic</li>
</ol>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Low risk malaria areas</li>
</ol>
<p>Endemic – Transmission is intense throughout the year e.g. coast, around Lake Victoria and Western region.</p>
<p>Seasonal transmission – Arid and semi arid areas. North and south eastern. Periods of transmission are short but intense especially when it rains.</p>
<p>Epidemic – Mostly found in the highlands. Others refer to it as highlands malaria.</p>
<p>Low risk malaria areas – Here they may experience imported malaria. This includes highlands of central region and Nairobi.</p>
<p>Facts about malaria in pregnancy.</p>
<ul>
<li>Pregnant woman suffer malaria easily compared to non pregnant women – lower immunity against malaria.</li>
<li>Many pregnant women may have malaria parasites but no symptoms.</li>
<li>Pregnancy makes woman lose their ability to fight malaria infection</li>
<li>Blood slide for mrdt may be negative despite malaria parasite being present as they tend to hide in placenta.</li>
<li>Malaria parasites may weaken placenta affecting the passage of nutrients and oxygen to the unborn baby lowering down its normal growth in terms of weight gain.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-malaria">Classification of malaria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-malaria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<p>Complicated malaria – No organ involvement</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-features-for-uncomplicated-malaria">Clinical features for uncomplicated malaria.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-features-for-uncomplicated-malaria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="national-guidelines-on-prevention-of-mip">National guidelines on prevention of MIP.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#national-guidelines-on-prevention-of-mip" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The government has put into measures to ensure that malaria is prevented during pregnancy. This is in line with world health organization recommendations. These measures are;</p>
<p>i. Administration of IPT with SP - sulphurdoxine pyremethymine.
ii. Provision of LLTN
iii. Prompt diagnosis and treatment of MIP
iv. Public health measures e.g. health education.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="administration-of-sp-as-ipt">Administration of SP as IPT.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#administration-of-sp-as-ipt" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Should be administered after quickening and after every 4 weeks till 40 weeks. Late dosing may be beneficial for woman presenting themselves late in pregnancy.</li>
<li>Should be given as DOT.</li>
<li>A minimum of 2 doses should be administered at interval of at least 4 weeks.</li>
<li>High dose of folic acid tablets to be administered 2 weeks after SP. Low dose folic acid can be administered together with SP.</li>
<li>HIV positive women on prophylaxis with daily clotrimoxazole should not be given SP.</li>
<li>HIV positive pregnant women taking antiretroviral therapy who are not on cotrimoxazole should receive SP.</li>
<li>Women who are known HIV positive or with unknown status and residing in area with high prevalence of HIV should receive at least 3 doses of SP.</li>
<li>SP should not be given to women who are allergic to sulphur.</li>
<li>If allergic to SP strengthen malaria preventive measures.</li>
<li>Should be used with ITN, haematenics and deworming.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="long-lasting-insecticidal-nets">Long lasting insecticidal nets<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#long-lasting-insecticidal-nets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>All pregnant women from malaria endemic areas should sleep under 11tn.</li>
<li>It is given free of charge in government health facilities during the first anc visit.</li>
<li>Teach the women on how to hand the net.</li>
<li>Encourage the woman to sleep under the net each and every night.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="side-effects">Side effects<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Hypoglycemia.</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Tinnitus, deafness, visual disturbances</li>
<li>Skin rushes</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
5 studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>Fever and dyspnoea</li>
<li>GIT disturbances i.e. nausea and vomiting.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-mip">Management of MIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-mip" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>☑ Admit or manage as outpatient depending on the condition.</li>
<li>☑ Reassure</li>
<li>☑ Administer paracetamol 1 gm</li>
<li>☑ Provide net</li>
<li>☑ Give oral iron tabs, stop folic for one week and thereafter</li>
<li>☑ Take adequate oral fluid</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="uncomplicated-malaria">Uncomplicated malaria<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#uncomplicated-malaria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1st-trimester">1st trimester<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1st-trimester" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Oral quinine 600mgs three times a day for 7 days.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Note</strong>- Don't with hold artemether- lumefantrine (AL) or any other drug if quinine is not available. However safety of the other drugs in 1st trimester to the fetus is not known. However the woman can lose life if left untreated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="treatment-in-2nd-and-3rd-trimester">Treatment in 2nd and 3rd Trimester<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-in-2nd-and-3rd-trimester" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>☐ Administer full dose of AL</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="supportive-care">Supportive care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#supportive-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Prevent hypoglycemia</li>
<li>monitor fetal condition</li>
<li>treat anaemia</li>
<li>antipyretics</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="management-of-complicated-severe-malaria">Management of complicated/ severe malaria.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-complicated-severe-malaria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Once diagnosis of complicated or severe malaria is made, this is a <strong>medical emergency</strong>. The life of both the mother and her baby are in danger.</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Pre- referral management</p>
<ul>
<li>Treatment of pregnant woman with complicated malaria should be started in bemonc facilities even when waiting for referral.</li>
<li>Administer I.M. or I.V. artesunate 2.4mg/kg or I.M. quinine 20mg/kg to a maximum of 1200mg a loading dose or I.M. artemether 160mg start.</li>
<li>A heath care provider should accompany the Patient to the next level of care.</li>
<li>Patients with altered level of consciousness should receive parenteral antibiotics (ceftriaxone) alongside antimalarials.</li>
</ul>
<p>Supportive care</p>
<ul>
<li>Admit and reassure</li>
<li>Rx can be quinine or artesunate.</li>
<li>Antipyretics are administered.</li>
<li>Monitor vital signs of the both the mother and the fetus</li>
<li>Monitor input and input</li>
<li>Expose the patient in case of fever.</li>
<li>Ensure provision of balanced diet if patient can take orally. This takes care of the hypoglycemia especially for those on oral quinine.</li>
<li>Monitor FHR and mother’s level of consciousness.</li>
<li>Monitor blood glucose level as it may fall. Quinine administration is associated with hypoglycemia.</li>
<li>If on quinine administered in a drip ensure the drug is not exposed to direct light.</li>
<li>Treatment for anaemia</li>
<li>Monitor signs of labour</li>
</ul>
<p>Administer artesunate – As first line</p>
<ul>
<li>Establish if initial dose has been given, if not administer IV artesunate 2.4 mg/kg.</li>
</ul>
<p>This document is available on
studocu
Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ul>
<li>12 hours from commencement of initial dose, start administering maintenance dose of artesunate 1.2 Mg/kg followed by 1.2 mg/kg OD till patient can take orally.</li>
<li>Once the patient is able to take oral administer a full dose of oral quinine.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="if-artesunate-is-not-available-administer-quinine-as-second-line-treatment">If artesunate is not available administer quinine - As second line treatment.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#if-artesunate-is-not-available-administer-quinine-as-second-line-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Establish if loading dose has been given; if not administer a loading dose of 20 mg/kg IV in 5% dextrose as infusion.</li>
<li>Give maintenance dose 8 hrs from commencement of initial dose at 10 mg/kg in dextrose solution</li>
<li>Repeat 10 mg/kg every 8 hrs until Patient can take orally.</li>
<li>When patient is able to take orally change to AL. Administer complete dose of AL.</li>
<li>A maximum of 3 mls should be used in each site of injection, if it exceeds another site should be used.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment-during-2nd-trimester-and-3rd-trimester">Treatment during 2nd trimester and 3rd trimester<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment-during-2nd-trimester-and-3rd-trimester" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>As for 1st trimester</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="anaemia-in-pregnacy">ANAEMIA IN PREGNACY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anaemia-in-pregnacy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Anaemia is defined as reduction in oxygen carrying capacity (Hb) of &lt; 11 g/dl.</p>
<p>Severe anaemia is Hb of &lt; 7 g/dl.</p>
<p>Severe anaemia can cause maternal death.</p>
<p>a pregnant woman with Hb of &lt; 7 g/dl is considered severely anaemic.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<p>Many factors interfere with normal RBC reproduction.</p>
<p>This includes,</p>
<ul>
<li>Deficiency of specific nutrients in the diet or</li>
<li>From inability of the body to absorb nutrients.</li>
<li>Dugs that interfere with absorption of nutrients e.g. anti convulsant interfere with folic acid absorption.</li>
<li>Excessive loss of RBC in hemorrhage</li>
<li>Excessive destruction of RBS from infection and inherited conditions e.g. SCD produce abnormal HB and leading to haemolysis of RBC</li>
<li>Pregnancy - During pregnancy blood volume increase. Increase in the plasma volume is greater than increase in the number of RBCs making blood less viscous and a fewer RBC in blood reducing concentration of hemoglobin leading to a condition known as <strong>physiological anemia</strong> in pregnancy.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Blood loss from <em>aph</em></li>
<li>Pregnancy itself. Multiple pregnancy, frequent minor disorders e.g. pica, hyperemesis, and physiological haemodilution.</li>
<li>Poor absorption may be due to drugs, hookworms and malaria.</li>
<li>Infestation: hookworms suck blood and prevent nutrients absorption.</li>
<li>Malaria</li>
<li>Iron and folate deficiency (due to poor dietary intake)</li>
<li>Vitamin B12 deficiency</li>
<li>Increased demand due to pregnancy</li>
<li>Hookworm infestation (increases blood loss)</li>
<li>Bone marrow suppression</li>
</ol>
<p>This document is available on</p>
<p>s  studocu</p>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>
<ol start="11">
<li>Advanced HIV infection</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: Iron deficiency anaemia is the most common cause of anaemia in pregnancy. &gt; 90% Of the cases.</p>
<p>Risk factors.</p>
<ul>
<li>Young primigravidas.</li>
<li>Poor socio-economic status.</li>
<li>Pre pregnancy anaemia</li>
<li>Multiple pregnancy</li>
<li>Frequency of pregnancy.</li>
<li>Chronic diseases e.g. HIV, Sickle cell.</li>
<li>Not attending health care.</li>
<li>excessive vomiting due to morning sickness</li>
<li>Smoking</li>
</ul>
<p>Classification of anaemia in pregnancy.
Mild anaemia – Hb 8–10.5g/dl
Moderate anaemia – Hb 7–8 gm/dl.
Severe anaemia – Hb &lt; 7g/dl.</p>
<p>Types of anemia during pregnancy</p>
<ul>
<li>Iron deficiency anemia</li>
<li>Folic acid deficiency anemia</li>
<li>Vitamin B12 deficiency anemia</li>
</ul>
<p>Effects of pregnancy in anaemia</p>
<ul>
<li>☑ Worsen due to haemodilution</li>
<li>☑ There is increase morbidity and mortality in severe cases.</li>
<li>☑ Minor disorders of pregnancy may mislead diagnosis of anaemia.</li>
</ul>
<p>Downloaded by Patrick Ngobiro (<a href="mailto:pngobiro@gmail.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">pngobiro@gmail.com</a>)</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-anaemia-to-the-mother">Effects of anaemia to the mother<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-anaemia-to-the-mother" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Poor maternal health.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Risk of abortion.
<span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">✓</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\checkmark</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6922em;"></span><span class="mord amsrm">✓</span></span></span></span></span>  Reduced resistance to infection.

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Pallor</li>
<li>Fatigue</li>
<li>Paleness of mucous membrane</li>
<li>Awareness of fast heartbeats (palpitations)</li>
<li>Tiredness</li>
<li>Breathlessness</li>
<li>Poor cap refill</li>
<li>increased respiratory rate</li>
<li>Headache</li>
<li>Dizziness</li>
<li>Pica</li>
<li>Lethargy</li>
<li>Prominent neck vein</li>
<li>Feeling of pins and needles on hand</li>
<li>Oedema of lower limbs</li>
<li>Spoon shaped nails incase of iron deficiency</li>
<li>Numbness.</li>
<li>Postural hypotension.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnosis">Diagnosis.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<p>THREE approaches in management of anaemia in pregnancy</p>
